\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dushanbe&action=edit&section=25 "Edit section: Electricity")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/The_tallest_dam_in_the_world_-_304_m_%28984_ft%29_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-The_tallest_dam_in_the_world_-_304_m_%28984_ft%29_-_panoramio.jpg)](/wiki/File:The_tallest_dam_in_the_world_-_304_m_(984_ft)_-_panoramio.jpg) Nurek Dam

In the 1930s, the use of [hydroelectricity](/wiki/Hydroelectricity "Hydroelectricity") began to take off in Dushanbe, leading it to be one of the most advanced in terms of [energy production in the Soviet Union](/wiki/Energy_in_the_Soviet_Union "Energy in the Soviet Union") at the time; today, 96% of Tajikistan's power comes from hydroelectricity.^[\[176\]](#cite_note-Bankwatch-2020-180)^^[\[177\]](#cite_note-ИМРӮЗ-1520-181)^ In Dushanbe, 990 million kWh were generated in 1980 which reached 1161 million kWh in 1985 but decreased significantly in 2001.^[\[178\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004d-182)^{#cite_ref-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004d_182-0}

In 2007, there was a major energy crisis because of the cold winter in Dushanbe that rendered Dushanbe's Soviet-era [energy system](/wiki/List_of_power_stations_in_Tajikistan "List of power stations in Tajikistan") ineffective and caused a severe crisis due to lack of heating.^[\[179\]](#cite_note-183)^ Since 2007, there have been energy shortages during the winter in Dushanbe.^[\[180\]](#cite_note-184)^ In 2009, Tajikistan's energy trade with other countries was suspended, and in 2012, natural gas imports from Uzbekistan were cut off, which further exacerbated the crisis, although the natural gas imports were restored in 2018.^[\[181\]](#cite_note-185)^ The [Nurek hydroelectric dam](/wiki/Nurek_Dam "Nurek Dam"), as of 2016, provides around 3/4 of the country's power.^[\[182\]](#cite_note-186)^ New hydroelectric plants are being planned^[\[183\]](#cite_note-187)^ and in 2017, the government proclaimed an end to the rolling blackouts;^[\[177\]](#cite_note-ИМРӮЗ-1520-181)^ however, in 2020, rolling blackouts continued.^[\[184\]](#cite_note-188)^ [Barqi Tojik](/wiki/Barqi_Tojik "Barqi Tojik") is the major energy producer for the city and produces 75% of the electricity in the country.^[\[185\]](#cite_note-189)^ To alleviate the energy crisis, a second coal plant for the city is planned with extensive Chinese involvement, but has been criticized for pollution and negative environmental effects.^[\[176\]](#cite_note-Bankwatch-2020-180)^{#cite_ref-Bankwatch-2020_180-1}

Varzob's three power plants generated 150 million kWh per year in 2004, and Dushanbe's power supply, built on the idea of a double ring, has an outer ring of power transmission lines from [Nurek Dam](/wiki/Nurek_Dam "Nurek Dam") to Dushanbe to [Yovon](/wiki/Yovon "Yovon") at a voltage of 220 kW and an inner ring which covers the perimeter of the city and consists of 110 kW power lines.^[\[178\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004d-182)^{#cite_ref-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004d_182-1}  

### Water and sanitation {#Water_and_sanitation}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dushanbe&action=edit&section=26 "Edit section: Water and sanitation")\]

Tajikistan has the highest average annual precipitation in its region, along with numerous rivers, natural lakes (such as [Lake Karakul](/wiki/Karakul_(Tajikistan) "Karakul (Tajikistan)")), and glaciers. Most of the outdated Dushanbe water system was built during the Soviet era in 1932 and not significantly expanded afterwards even with a rising population.^[\[186\]](#cite_note-190)^ The Big Gissar Canal was constructed in 1942 and irrigates much of southern Tajikistan and goes from the [Kofarnihon river](/wiki/Kofarnihon_River "Kofarnihon River") to the [Surxondaryo](/wiki/Surxondaryo_River "Surxondaryo River").^[\[187\]](#cite_note-191)^ As of 2004, the length of the city's water supply network was 476 km (296 mi) and mainly got its water from the [Varzob](/wiki/Varzob_District "Varzob District"), [Kofarnikhon](/wiki/Kofarnihon_River "Kofarnihon River") and the South-West.^[\[188\]](#cite_note-192)^ Water is supplied through two ground and two surface water treatment plants.^[\[189\]](#cite_note-CDC-1998-193)^ As of 2018, 40% of the city's population did not have access to sewage systems.^[\[190\]](#cite_note-194)^{#cite_ref-194}  

### Parks {#Parks}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dushanbe&action=edit&section=27 "Edit section: Parks")\]

As of 2020, there are 15 parks in Dushanbe.^[\[191\]](#cite_note-195)^ One of the most well known is Rudaki Park, created in the mid-1930s along with a bronze statue of Lenin.^[\[192\]](#cite_note-196)^ The park was renovated in 2007.^[\[193\]](#cite_note-197)^ Another park is [Victory Park](/wiki/Victory_Park,_Dushanbe "Victory Park, Dushanbe"), which was created in 1975 to commemorate the Great Patriotic War.^[\[194\]](#cite_note-198)^ The Botanical Garden of the Academy of Sciences of Tajikistan was founded in 1933, and trees planted then are still prominent in the park. In 2007 a collection of [folk architecture](/wiki/Folk_architecture "Folk architecture") was added the park.^[\[195\]](#cite_note-199)^{#cite_ref-199}

* Parks in Dushanbe
  * [![Rudaki Park with the Palace of the Nation in the background.](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Ustod_Rudaki_Park_and_Palace_of_the_Nation_in_Dushanbe_-_panoramio.jpg/190px-Ustod_Rudaki_Park_and_Palace_of_the_Nation_in_Dushanbe_-_panoramio.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ustod_Rudaki_Park_and_Palace_of_the_Nation_in_Dushanbe_-_panoramio.jpg "Rudaki Park with the Palace of the Nation in the background.")  
  Rudaki Park with the Palace of the Nation in the background.
  * [![Folk architecture area of the botanical gardens](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/%D0%9B%D0%BE%D1%88%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8C_%D0%B8_%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B0_01.jpg/150px-%D0%9B%D0%BE%D1%88%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8C_%D0%B8_%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B0_01.jpg)](/wiki/File:%D0%9B%D0%BE%D1%88%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8C_%D0%B8_%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B0_01.jpg "Folk architecture area of the botanical gardens")  
  Folk architecture area of the botanical gardens
  * [![Dushanbe botanical gardens](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Botanical_gardens_2_-_panoramio.jpg/190px-Botanical_gardens_2_-_panoramio.jpg)](/wiki/File:Botanical_gardens_2_-_panoramio.jpg "Dushanbe botanical gardens")  
  Dushanbe botanical gardens
  * [![A parade in Victory Park](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/%D0%A0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B0%D1%89%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%8F%D0%BB%D0%B8_%D1%83%D1%87%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%B2_%D0%BF%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B5_%D0%B2_%D0%A2%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B5_02.jpg/190px-%D0%A0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B0%D1%89%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%8F%D0%BB%D0%B8_%D1%83%D1%87%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%B2_%D0%BF%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B5_%D0%B2_%D0%A2%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B5_02.jpg)](/wiki/File:%D0%A0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B0%D1%89%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%8F%D0%BB%D0%B8_%D1%83%D1%87%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%B2_%D0%BF%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B5_%D0%B2_%D0%A2%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B5_02.jpg "A parade in Victory Park")  
  A parade in Victory Park
  * [![World War 2 memorial in Victory Park](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/World_war_2_memorial%2C_victory_park_%282%29_-_panoramio.jpg/190px-World_war_2_memorial%2C_victory_park_%282%29_-_panoramio.jpg)](/wiki/File:World_war_2_memorial,_victory_park_(2)_-_panoramio.jpg "World War 2 memorial in Victory Park")  
  World War 2 memorial in Victory Park

### Cemeteries {#Cemeteries}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dushanbe&action=edit&section=28 "Edit section: Cemeteries")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Mausoleum_of_Sadriddin_Ayni.of_Dushanbe_08.jpg/220px-Mausoleum_of_Sadriddin_Ayni.of_Dushanbe_08.jpg)](/wiki/File:Mausoleum_of_Sadriddin_Ayni.of_Dushanbe_08.jpg) Mausoleum of Sadriddin Ayni

There are 5 main and 14 unrecognized cemeteries in Dushanbe.^[\[196\]](#cite_note-asiaplustj-2020b-200)^ One of the 5 mains ones is Mekhrobod, founded in 2013, that consists of 74 acres of primarily tombstones. For a period of 9 months in 2019, 78 people were buried there. Luchob cemetery, also one of the five, uses commemorative [steles](/wiki/Stele "Stele") to remember the dead and houses more well-known figures. As of October 2019, 54 people were buried there such as [Jabbor Rasulov](/wiki/Jabbor_Rasulov "Jabbor Rasulov"), [Bobojon Ghafurov](/wiki/Bobojon_Ghafurov "Bobojon Ghafurov"), [Muhammad Osimi](/wiki/Muhammad_Osimi "Muhammad Osimi"), [Mirzo Tursunzade](/wiki/Mirzo_Tursunzoda "Mirzo Tursunzoda"), [Loik Sherali](/wiki/Loiq_Sher-Ali "Loiq Sher-Ali"), [Muhammadjon Shakuri](/wiki/Muhammadjon_Shakuri "Muhammadjon Shakuri"), [Malika Sabirova](/wiki/Malika_Sobirova "Malika Sobirova"), [Tufa Fozylova](/wiki/Tuhfa_Fozilova "Tuhfa Fozilova"), and [Mukaddima Ashrafi](/wiki/Muqadamma_Ashrafi "Muqadamma Ashrafi"). It was founded in 1977 and uses the smallest amount of land of the five.^[\[196\]](#cite_note-asiaplustj-2020b-200)^ In 2017, the government secretly moved many national figures from Aini park to Luchob cemetery, sparking outrage.^[\[197\]](#cite_note-201)^{#cite_ref-201}

Sari Osiyo, founded in 1933, is another one of the five cemeteries. It is one of the oldest in the city and has graves from the late 19th century. For the 9-month period in 2019, 225 were buried here. The Christian cemetery is another one of the five, the least visited although frequented by the [201st Russian division](/wiki/Russian_201st_Military_Base "Russian 201st Military Base"). It uses 84.3 hectares of land and saw 197 new graves over the same nine-month period. Shokhmansur is the last of the five main cemeteries and saw 65 burials over the 9-month period.^[\[196\]](#cite_note-asiaplustj-2020b-200)^ The Jewish cemetery of the city, one of the fourteen unofficial ones, is looked after by the Congress of [Bukharian Jews](/wiki/Bukharan_Jews "Bukharan Jews").^[\[198\]](#cite_note-202)^{#cite_ref-202}  

### Healthcare {#Healthcare}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dushanbe&action=edit&section=29 "Edit section: Healthcare")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Big_Hospital.jpg/220px-Big_Hospital.jpg)](/wiki/File:Big_Hospital.jpg) Istiqlol Medical Complex

In 1925, Dushanbe city hospital and the [ambulance](/wiki/Ambulance "Ambulance") system was created, and numerous medical facilities sprung up during the decade. In 1939, an infectious disease hospital was created and in the same year the [Stalinabad Medical Institute](/wiki/Avicenna_Tajik_State_Medical_University "Avicenna Tajik State Medical University") was founded. During World War 2 up to the Tajik Civil War, the healthcare system significantly expanded through hospitals and specialized clinics.^[\[199\]](#cite_note-203)^{#cite_ref-203}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Sanatorium_Khodjaobigarm_01.jpg/220px-Sanatorium_Khodjaobigarm_01.jpg)](/wiki/File:Sanatorium_Khodjaobigarm_01.jpg) Khoja Obi Garm sanatorium

[Tajikistan's health care system](/wiki/Health_in_Tajikistan "Health in Tajikistan") is concentrated in Dushanbe.^[\[200\]](#cite_note-204)^ There is a well-developed network of city [clinics](/wiki/Clinic "Clinic"), [hospitals](/wiki/Hospital "Hospital"), medical centers, [maternity hospitals](/wiki/Maternity_hospital "Maternity hospital"), [orphanages](/wiki/Orphanage "Orphanage"), sanitary and [epidemiological](/wiki/Epidemiology "Epidemiology") centers - a total of 62 medical institutions in the city as of spring 2010. These 62 treatment and prevention facilities include 17 hospitals, 2 orphanages, 14 city health centers, 5 dental clinics, 8 centers of sanitary and epidemiological surveillance and disincentives, 12 city branch centers and 4 support centers.^[\[201\]](#cite_note-205)^ In 2019, the number of hospitals grew to 43.^[\[5\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe-2021a-5)^ Primary health care for Dushanbe residents (and guests of the city) is provided in 39 institutions (city health centers, [dental clinics](/wiki/Dental_clinic "Dental clinic"), centers for sanitary and epidemiological surveillance and de-stations, city branch centers).^[\[202\]](#cite_note-206)^{#cite_ref-206}

Among the main [medical institutions of Dushanbe](/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_Tajikistan "List of hospitals in Tajikistan") are specialized republican hospitals and centers, city polyclinics No. 1-5, the city infectious diseases hospital, the children's infectious diseases hospital, and the departmental hospitals of the country's power ministries.^[\[203\]](#cite_note-207)^ Citizens receive care through their assigned clinics in the city.^[\[189\]](#cite_note-CDC-1998-193)^ Some hospitals in Dushanbe include the Mansurov Clinic, the Tajik Railways Hospital, the Shifobakhsh National Medical Center, and the Istiqlol Medical Complex.^[\[204\]](#cite_note-208)^ Khoja Obi Garm, a Soviet-era [sanatorium](/wiki/Sanatorium "Sanatorium"), still is in operation today and uses [radon](/wiki/Radon "Radon") treatments, among others.^[\[205\]](#cite_note-209)^ Temporary hospitals were established during the [COVID-19 pandemic](/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic "COVID-19 pandemic").^[\[206\]](#cite_note-210)^{#cite_ref-210}  

Economy {#Economy}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dushanbe&action=edit&section=30 "Edit section: Economy")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/%D0%9E%D1%84%D0%B8%D1%81_%D0%90%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%B0.jpg/220px-%D0%9E%D1%84%D0%B8%D1%81_%D0%90%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%B0.jpg)](/wiki/File:%D0%9E%D1%84%D0%B8%D1%81_%D0%90%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%B0.jpg) Bank in Dushanbe

In 2018, the [gross regional product](/wiki/Gross_regional_product "Gross regional product") (GRP) of Dushanbe was 13,808,000,000 [somoni](/wiki/Tajikistani_somoni "Tajikistani somoni"), equaling approximately $1,508,900,000, with a growth rate of 7.3%. That comprised 20.1% of the overall [GDP](/wiki/GDP "GDP") of [Tajikistan](/wiki/Tajikistan "Tajikistan").^[\[207\]](#cite_note-211)^^[\[128\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe-2021b-132)^ In the first half of 2020, the GRP of Dushanbe was 20.7% of the GDP of the country.^[\[208\]](#cite_note-212)^ The average salary of the city as of 2014^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Dushanbe&action=edit)^ is 1402.67 somoni, or $147.18.^[\[87\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe-2020d-91)^ As the center of financial activity of the republic, Dushanbe housed more than 30 commercial banks in 2004.^[\[178\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004d-182)^{#cite_ref-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004d_182-2}

Dushanbe has extensive international trade. Exports from Dushanbe consisted of $8,343,200 during the first half of 2019,^[\[209\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe-2020b-213)^ and overall foreign trade turnover was $398,080,900 in 2018. The primary countries Dushanbe exports to are Turkey (42.8% of the total), Iran (28.0%), Russia (10.8%), Afghanistan (7.3%), China (1.2%), Poland (1.2%), and others. For imports, Russia makes up 54.5% of the total, Kazakhstan 13.5%, China 6.8%, Italy 3.4%, Turkey 2.6%, Turkmenistan 2.5%, Ukraine 2.1%, Iran 1.4%, the United Arab Emirates 1.2%, and others make up the rest.^[\[210\]](#cite_note-214)^{#cite_ref-214}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Dushanbe%2C_Tajikistan_-_panoramio_%28102%29.jpg/220px-Dushanbe%2C_Tajikistan_-_panoramio_%28102%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Dushanbe,_Tajikistan_-_panoramio_(102).jpg) Coal plant in Dushanbe

During and during the decade after the Soviet invasion, most industries were focused on meeting local demand with local materials. Meat packing, soap production, bricks, lumber, silk thread, leather, clothing, and generation of electric power were all local industries during the time period.^[\[61\]](#cite_note-Atkin-2020-65)^ In 1932, 776 workers were employed in industry, while in 1938, 12 thousand were.^[\[178\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004d-182)^ During World War 2, the city's industry grew significantly with the Soviet decision to relocate industry eastwards to cities like Dushanbe, specifically [light industries](/wiki/Light_industries "Light industries") like [textile manufacturing](/wiki/Textile_manufacturing "Textile manufacturing") and [food processing](/wiki/Food_processing "Food processing").^[\[61\]](#cite_note-Atkin-2020-65)^ Industry output increased by 2.5 times from 1940 to 1945.^[\[28\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004c-32)^ About 1/3 of the industrial and white-collar labor force of Tajikistan is located in Dushanbe, despite containing less than 10 percent of Tajikistan's population.^[\[61\]](#cite_note-Atkin-2020-65)^ From January to August 2019, there were 455 manufacturing companies in Dushanbe, producing 1,644,745,400 Somoni worth of products. The majority of that, 63.9%, was from the [processing industry](/wiki/Processing_industry "Processing industry"), 34.5% was from electricity, water, gas, and air purification, and the other 1.6% was from the non-metallic construction industry.^[\[209\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe-2020b-213)^ The industry produces over 300 types of products.^[\[211\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe-2020c-215)^ Exports from the industrial sector consisted of $1,535,500 during the time period.^[\[209\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe-2020b-213)^{#cite_ref-Dushanbe-2020b_213-2}

The main industrial products exported from the city are [cotton yarn](/wiki/Cotton_yarn "Cotton yarn"), finished [cotton fabrics](/wiki/Cotton_Fabric "Cotton Fabric"), [hosiery](/wiki/Hosiery "Hosiery"), cable products, [agricultural](/wiki/Agriculture "Agriculture") products, [tobacco](/wiki/Tobacco "Tobacco") products, and trade equipment, among others.^[\[211\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe-2020c-215)^ Industry, as of 2019, employed 20746 people, with an average salary of 1428.02 somoni.^[\[209\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe-2020b-213)^ [Light industry](/wiki/Light_industry "Light industry") is the most mature industry in the city, aided by the location of raw materials in the country. Some large companies in light industry are Nassoch, which processes large amounts of cotton fiber, Chevar and Guliston, which both produce garments, and Nafisa, which produces [hosiery](/wiki/Hosiery "Hosiery").^[\[211\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe-2020c-215)^ The [electrical](/wiki/Electronics_manufacturing_services "Electronics manufacturing services"), [engineering](/wiki/Industrial_engineering "Industrial engineering"), and [metallurgical](/wiki/Metallurgy "Metallurgy") industries are also prominent in the republic. Tajiktekstilmash, which produces varied products for agriculture and electricity, and Tajikcable, which produces cables, are two well known companies from that sector of the economy. Somon-Tachkhizot, which produces electronic goods, Torgmash, which produces goods for trading companies, and Valve Plant, which produces iron products are some other prominent companies in the industry.^[\[211\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe-2020c-215)^ The [food processing industry](/wiki/Food-processing_industry "Food-processing industry") also has a presence in the city with many [wineries](/wiki/Wineries "Wineries"), [dairy](/wiki/Dairy_farming "Dairy farming") and [meatpacking plants](/wiki/Meatpacking_plant "Meatpacking plant"), [canneries](/wiki/Canneries "Canneries"), and [bakeries](/wiki/Bakery "Bakery") all in the city. Various other industries exist in the city as well.^[\[211\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe-2020c-215)^ These include the building materials industry, which produces cement, oil (with 3 main gas deposits) and plastics;^[\[212\]](#cite_note-216)^ the wood industry; and the printing industry, which consists of 80% of the republic's capacity and began in 1926.^[\[178\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004d-182)^{#cite_ref-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004d_182-4}

In 2014, the retail sector was involved in 2.6 billion somoni of transactions. In the service sector, hotels, restaurants, canteens and cafes sold services worth 296.6 million somoni. The paid services of the city in 2014 amounted to 5662.2 somoni per capita.^[\[87\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe-2020d-91)^{#cite_ref-Dushanbe-2020d_91-3}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Dushanbe_2010_01_Hotel_Tajikistan.jpg/220px-Dushanbe_2010_01_Hotel_Tajikistan.jpg)](/wiki/File:Dushanbe_2010_01_Hotel_Tajikistan.jpg) Hotel Tajikistan

Dushanbe is the capital of tourism of the [Economic Cooperation Organization](/wiki/Economic_Cooperation_Organization "Economic Cooperation Organization") and is served by more than 40 hotels. The building of 9 modern hotels, with room for more than 1000 people, is being planned.^[\[213\]](#cite_note-217)^{#cite_ref-217}

In 2018 and 2019, numerous initiatives, such as Dushanbe becoming a member of the World Tourism Cities Federation, different festivals, legislation promoting the city, an art gallery, and the establishment of the Year of Tourism and Folk Crafts in 2018 all served to promote the tourism industry. The Dushanbe Summer Fest, another promoted festival, is notable for its internet connectivity.^[\[214\]](#cite_note-218)^^[\[215\]](#cite_note-219)^^[\[216\]](#cite_note-220)^ Compared with the rest of the country, however, Dushanbe is a less popular tourist destination, partially due to its relatively recent founding and lack of historical significance.^[\[217\]](#cite_note-221)^ Museums in the city include the [Tajikistan National Museum](/wiki/Tajikistan_National_Museum "Tajikistan National Museum"), founded in 1934,^[\[218\]](#cite_note-222)^ and the [Gurminj Museum of Musical Instruments](/wiki/Gurminj_Museum_of_Musical_Instruments "Gurminj Museum of Musical Instruments"), which contains Pamiri and Badakshani musical instruments.^[\[219\]](#cite_note-223)^{#cite_ref-223}  

Culture {#Culture}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dushanbe&action=edit&section=31 "Edit section: Culture")\]

Culture in Dushanbe, first developed during the period of Bukharan rule, grew under the Soviet Union, which established many of the first cultural institutions of the city. After independence, Dushanbe's culture went in a more nationalist direction.^[\[220\]](#cite_note-224)^{#cite_ref-224}  

### Performing arts {#Performing_arts}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dushanbe&action=edit&section=32 "Edit section: Performing arts")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%B2_%D0%B8%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BD%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B8_%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B1%D1%8B_%D0%9E%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%B8_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%A5%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0.jpg/220px-%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%B2_%D0%B8%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BD%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B8_%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B1%D1%8B_%D0%9E%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%B8_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%A5%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0.jpg)](/wiki/File:%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%B2_%D0%B8%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BD%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B8_%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B1%D1%8B_%D0%9E%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%B8_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%A5%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0.jpg) Shashmaqam in the Dushanbe Concert Hall

During the 19th century, [shashmaqam](/wiki/Shashmaqam "Shashmaqam") was the most prevalent musical genre in Tajikistan. While Soviet authorities labeled it as "music composed for the Emir" and repressed it, in modern times it has gained greater popularity.^[\[221\]](#cite_note-iias-2020-225)^{#cite_ref-iias-2020_225-0}

During the [Soviet period](/wiki/Tajik_SSR "Tajik SSR"), the [Soviet Union](/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union") encouraged the development of music in Dushanbe, a less culturally crowded place then typical [Russian megacities](/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Russia_by_population "List of cities in Russia by population"). Revolutionary songs, like the [Marseillaise](/wiki/La_Marseillaise "La Marseillaise"), were promoted and translated into Tajik.^[\[222\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004l-226)^ The Tajik Philharmonic Society was founded in 1938; today, it is named after Akasharif Juraev.^[\[223\]](#cite_note-227)^^[\[224\]](#cite_note-228)^ [Sergei Artemevich Balasanyan](/w/index.php?title=Sergei_Artemevich_Balasanyan&action=edit&redlink=1 "Sergei Artemevich Balasanyan (page does not exist)"), an [Armenian](/wiki/Armenian_SSR "Armenian SSR"), was one composer who originally went to Dushanbe from 1936--1943 to prepare the SSR for an upcoming Tajik cultural festival to be held in Moscow. While we was there, he described himself as a "composer, social-musical worker, [folklorist](/wiki/Folklorist "Folklorist"), and [pedagogue](/wiki/Pedagogy "Pedagogy")." He also became the head of the Tajik Composer's Union and the artistic lead of the opera house.^[\[221\]](#cite_note-iias-2020-225)^ Large numbers of Russian and Ukrainian symphonies moved to Dushanbe during World War 2.^[\[225\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004j-229)^{#cite_ref-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004j_229-0}

The [Tajik Opera and Ballet Theater](https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%A2%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%B8%D0%BA%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%80_%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%80%D1%8B_%D0%B8_%D0%B1%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B0 "ru:Таджикский театр оперы и балета"), whose building was named after [Sadriddin Ayni](/wiki/Sadriddin_Ayni "Sadriddin Ayni") and was the first opera house in Dushanbe, was founded in 1936.^[\[226\]](#cite_note-music-dic-2020-230)^^[\[227\]](#cite_note-OperaBalet-2020-231)^ The first opera performed, the first in history of Tajikistan, was The Vose Uprising and detailed a [peasants' revolt](/wiki/Peasants%27_Revolt "Peasants' Revolt") in eastern [Bukhara](/wiki/Emirate_of_Bukhara "Emirate of Bukhara") in the late 19th century.^[\[228\]](#cite_note-232)^ One notable singer of the opera was [Hanifa Mavlianova](/wiki/Hanifa_Mavlianova "Hanifa Mavlianova").^[\[229\]](#cite_note-Кино-Театр-2020-233)^{#cite_ref-Кино-Театр-2020_233-0}

Another musician to come to Dushanbe during the Soviet period was [Aleksandr Lensky](/wiki/Aleksandr_Lensky "Aleksandr Lensky"), a [Moldovan](/wiki/Moldavian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic") who came to Tajikistan in 1937. He was the artistic director of the Lahuti Theatre, director of the [Tajik Philharmonic](/w/index.php?title=Tajik_Philharmonic&action=edit&redlink=1 "Tajik Philharmonic (page does not exist)"), and first secretary of the Tajik Union of Composers. He also composed the first Tajik opera and many orchestral pieces.^[\[221\]](#cite_note-iias-2020-225)^ Another orchestra in Dushanbe is the [Opera Orchestra](/wiki/Opera_Orchestra_of_Dushanbe "Opera Orchestra of Dushanbe").^[\[230\]](#cite_note-234)^ The State Symphony Orchestra of Tajikistan was founded in 2016, and its first concert took place on 9 September 2016.^[\[231\]](#cite_note-235)^^[\[232\]](#cite_note-236)^ The Tajik Opera and Ballet Theater continues operating to this day and has won the [Order of Lenin](/wiki/Order_of_Lenin "Order of Lenin").^[\[226\]](#cite_note-music-dic-2020-230)^ At various times the opera house performed operas on modern, historical, national, revolutionary, and heroic themes.^[\[227\]](#cite_note-OperaBalet-2020-231)^{#cite_ref-OperaBalet-2020_231-1}

The Tajik Opera and Ballet Theater also had the first ballet performed in Dushanbe in 1941, entitled Two Roses, and the ballet troupe gradually grew over time.^[\[229\]](#cite_note-Кино-Театр-2020-233)^^[\[233\]](#cite_note-237)^ The troupe was improved with graduates from the [Leningrad Choreographic School](/wiki/Leningrad_Choreographic_School "Leningrad Choreographic School") with ballet dancers such as [Malika Sabirova](/wiki/Malika_Sobirova "Malika Sobirova").^[\[229\]](#cite_note-Кино-Театр-2020-233)^ The theater was refitted in 2009 and continues operating to this day.^[\[234\]](#cite_note-238)^{#cite_ref-238}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Ayni_Opera_Theatre%2C_Dushanbe%2C_Tajikistan.jpg/220px-Ayni_Opera_Theatre%2C_Dushanbe%2C_Tajikistan.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ayni_Opera_Theatre,_Dushanbe,_Tajikistan.jpg) Ayni Opera theater

The 1920s saw the birth of drama in the city. The first, Lahouti theater, was built in 1929. In the 1930s, Soviet themes like class struggle, fighting against the past, and gender equality were prominent in plays. In 1935, the Tajik Musical Theater, now the Ayni theater, was built.^[\[225\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004j-229)^^[\[235\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004i-239)^ A comedy troupe was created in 1944 and after the war young artists influenced plays in Dushanbe, influencing the creation of the Tajik State Youth Theater.^[\[225\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004j-229)^{#cite_ref-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004j_229-2}

Continuing with a nationalist tradition, Tajik classics were made into plays. During World War 2, plays were focused on the war and historical themes from the 1950s onward. In the 70s and 80s foreign plays, like [Oedipus Rex](/wiki/Oedipus_Rex "Oedipus Rex"), were introduced to Dushanbe. After independence, plays focused primarily on the devastating civil war.^[\[235\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004i-239)^^[\[225\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004j-229)^ Today, some theaters are the Tajik Academic Opera and Ballet Theater, the State Russian Drama Theater, the youth theater, the State Experimental Theater, and the republican puppet theater.^[\[225\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004j-229)^{#cite_ref-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004j_229-4}

The [Mayakovsky Theatre](/wiki/Mayakovsky_Theatre_(Dushanbe) "Mayakovsky Theatre (Dushanbe)") was Tajikistan's oldest theatre and last surviving Russian-language theatre company; it was demolished in 2016 as part of the government's wholesale destruction of numerous 20th-century buildings of historical and architectural interest.^[\[236\]](#cite_note-240)^{#cite_ref-240}  

### Literature {#Literature}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dushanbe&action=edit&section=33 "Edit section: Literature")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ae/Mirsaid-mirshakar.jpg)](/wiki/File:Mirsaid-mirshakar.jpg) Mirsaid Mirshakar

The first printing press in Tajikistan was created in August 1924, the Tajik State Publishing House, the Donish Publishing House was founded in 1944.^[\[237\]](#cite_note-Mulloev-2009-241)^ In 1925 4 books were printed, which grew to 13 in 1926. In 1930, Sadriddin Ayni wrote the first Tajik novel, Dokhunda.^[\[238\]](#cite_note-242)^ Publishing houses established in 1934 and the Academy of Sciences of Tajikistan publishing house dramatically increased book production in the city.^[\[239\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004g-243)^ The Maorif Publishing House was created in 1975.^[\[237\]](#cite_note-Mulloev-2009-241)^ In 2004, there were 30 publishing companies in the city.^[\[239\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004g-243)^{#cite_ref-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004g_243-1}

Dushanbe became the center of Tajik literature in the 1920s with figures such as [Sadriddin Ayni](/wiki/Sadriddin_Ayni "Sadriddin Ayni"), [Abolqasem Lahouti](/wiki/Abolqasem_Lahouti "Abolqasem Lahouti"), and [Payrav Sulaymoni](/wiki/Payrav_Sulaymoni "Payrav Sulaymoni") along with new Soviet literature calling for revolution and social equality and Tajik nationalist literature. Children's books and translated works also had their beginnings in this period. In the 1930s, young Russian writers influenced the literature of the city, part of the "Komsomol generation." The themes often touched on the rapid development of Dushanbe during the 30s.^[\[235\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004i-239)^{#cite_ref-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004i_239-2}

During World War 2, literature shifted towards patriotic and militaristic themes of protecting the motherland in shorter formats than novels. Messages from the frontlines and satires became popular. Russian literature also became known, partially due to the movement of factories and people from the [frontlines of the war](/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II) "Eastern Front (World War II)") to the east. After the war, prose works and poetry, with poets like [Mirzo Tursunzoda](/wiki/Mirzo_Tursunzoda "Mirzo Tursunzoda"), became more popular along with the continuation of genres from previous decades. Literary criticism developed along with analysis of individual writers.^[\[235\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004i-239)^{#cite_ref-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004i_239-3}

From the 1950s, the historical revolutionary genre developed, prompting authors to use history for inspiration. In the 60s the new genre of science fiction began in the city with writers like [Mirsaid Mirshakar](/wiki/Mirsaid_Mirshakar "Mirsaid Mirshakar"). In the 70s and 80s the themes of disorder gained more prominence, not coincidentally soon before the Soviet Union's collapse. In poetry, civic and philosophical lyrical themes were most popular.^[\[235\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004i-239)^ After independence, previously forbidden subjects like religion started to appear in literature, along with reflections on the civil war and a more international scene has developed in the city.^[\[235\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004i-239)^{#cite_ref-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004i_239-5}  

### Visual arts {#Visual_arts}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dushanbe&action=edit&section=34 "Edit section: Visual arts")\]

Sculpture was first introduced to Dushanbe in the 1920s and throughout the Soviet period was focused on combining modern culture and a classical heritage. Modern sculpture mainly has historical subjects like [Firdavsi](/wiki/Ferdowsi "Ferdowsi"), [Shah Anushirvan](/wiki/Khosrow_I "Khosrow I"), or [Ismail Samani](/wiki/Ismail_Samani "Ismail Samani"), often to commemorate Tajik nationhood and ethnicity by looking to past Achaemenid and Samanid figures.^[\[131\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004k-135)^^[\[66\]](#cite_note-Hughes-2017-70)^{#cite_ref-Hughes-2017_70-3}

* Statues in Dushanbe
  * [![Statue of Rudaki](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/-Rudaki_in_Park_Dushanbe_city.jpg/170px--Rudaki_in_Park_Dushanbe_city.jpg)](/wiki/File:-Rudaki_in_Park_Dushanbe_city.jpg "Statue of Rudaki")  
  Statue of [Rudaki](/wiki/Rudaki "Rudaki")
  * [![Statue of Omar Khayyam](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/%D0%A3%D0%BC%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B8_%D0%A5%D0%B0%D0%B9%D1%91%D0%BC_%284%29.jpg/170px-%D0%A3%D0%BC%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B8_%D0%A5%D0%B0%D0%B9%D1%91%D0%BC_%284%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:%D0%A3%D0%BC%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B8_%D0%A5%D0%B0%D0%B9%D1%91%D0%BC_(4).jpg "Statue of Omar Khayyam")  
  Statue of [Omar Khayyam](/wiki/Omar_Khayyam "Omar Khayyam")
  * [![Statue of Lenin](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Soviet_monument_to_Lenin.Dushanbe.jpg/127px-Soviet_monument_to_Lenin.Dushanbe.jpg)](/wiki/File:Soviet_monument_to_Lenin.Dushanbe.jpg "Statue of Lenin")  
  Statue of [Lenin](/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin "Vladimir Lenin")
  * [![Statue of Avicenna](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/%D0%9C%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%83%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%82_%D0%90%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B5.JPG/170px-%D0%9C%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%83%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%82_%D0%90%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B5.JPG)](/wiki/File:%D0%9C%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%83%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%82_%D0%90%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B5.JPG "Statue of Avicenna")  
  Statue of [Avicenna](/wiki/Avicenna "Avicenna")

Painting in Dushanbe took off when Russian painters moved to this city in the 20s and 30s. By the 50s, Tajik artists started to paint. In the 1960s, the severe style \[[ru](https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%A1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BB%D1%8C "ru:Суровый стиль")\] grew and in the 70s and 80s a focus on [Tajik heritage](/wiki/History_of_Tajikistan "History of Tajikistan") and [nationalism](/wiki/Nationalism "Nationalism") was predominant. In the late 80s, however, painting shifted from a focus on historical figures to emotional depth and personality. During the civil war, a theme of conflict in painting developed.^[\[131\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004k-135)^ Sabzali Sharipov's black and white series, for example, was devoted to the civil war.^[\[240\]](#cite_note-244)^{#cite_ref-244}  

### Film {#Film}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dushanbe&action=edit&section=35 "Edit section: Film")\]  
See also: [Cinema of Tajikistan](/wiki/Cinema_of_Tajikistan "Cinema of Tajikistan")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/%D0%9A%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B8_%D0%92%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD.jpg/220px-%D0%9A%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B8_%D0%92%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD.jpg)](/wiki/File:%D0%9A%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B8_%D0%92%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD.jpg) Movie theater

Cinema in Dushanbe started in the 1930s with the creation of film studios and cinemas by the Soviet government, although the first cinema was created in 1927 where residents watched Nibelung by [Frits Lang](/wiki/Fritz_Lang "Fritz Lang"). [Komil Yarmatov](/wiki/Kamil_Yarmatov "Kamil Yarmatov") was the first prominent Tajik film director. Documentaries were also popular in this period, and the first feature film appeared in 1938. In World War 2, [feature film](/wiki/Feature_film "Feature film") production in Dushanbe was suspended due to lack of supplies. After the war, more feature films were developed, with many movies attempting to create a portrait of the city. In the 1980s a new generation of filmmakers brought new values such a pluralism into the theater, which led to some films focusing on the truth of Soviet history. During the civil war, the landscape changed dramatically. [Tajikfilm](/wiki/Tajikfilm "Tajikfilm"), which formerly had a monopoly on filmmaking, had to shut down, while independent filmmakers chronicled the horrors of the civil war.^[\[222\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004l-226)^^[\[241\]](#cite_note-245)^{#cite_ref-245}  

### Sports {#Sports}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dushanbe&action=edit&section=36 "Edit section: Sports")\]

Gymnastics, equestrian sports and athletics were practiced in 1923 at the Dushanbe sports club and in 1929 tennis was introduced. The All-Tajik [Spartakiad](/wiki/Spartakiad "Spartakiad") was first held in 1934, and in 1939 [Dynamo Dushanbe](/wiki/Dynamo_Dushanbe "Dynamo Dushanbe") won the quarterfinals of the [Cup of the USSR](/wiki/Soviet_Cup "Soviet Cup"). In 1950 the country's soccer team took first place in the [Central Asian Games](/wiki/Central_Asian_Games "Central Asian Games").^[\[242\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004m-246)^{#cite_ref-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004m_246-0}

In 2003, Dushanbe hosted the [Central Asian Games](/wiki/2003_Central_Asian_Games "2003 Central Asian Games"). The most popular sports in Dushanbe are [sambo](/wiki/Sambo_(martial_art) "Sambo (martial art)"), [wrestling](/wiki/Wrestling "Wrestling"), [judo](/wiki/Judo "Judo"), [karate](/wiki/Karate "Karate"), [taekwondo](/wiki/Taekwondo "Taekwondo"), [artistic gymnastics](/wiki/Artistic_gymnastics "Artistic gymnastics"), [weightlifting](/wiki/Weightlifting_(sport) "Weightlifting (sport)"), [archery](/wiki/Archery "Archery"), [shooting](/wiki/Shooting_sports "Shooting sports"), [boxing](/wiki/Boxing "Boxing"), [football](/wiki/Soccer "Soccer"), [basketball](/wiki/Basketball "Basketball"), [diving](/wiki/Diving_(sport) "Diving (sport)"), [tennis](/wiki/Tennis "Tennis"), [chess](/wiki/Chess "Chess"), [Buzkashi](/wiki/Buzkashi "Buzkashi"), and [checkers](/wiki/Checkers "Checkers").^[\[242\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004m-246)^ Four soccer teams of the [Tajikistan Higher League](/wiki/Tajikistan_Higher_League "Tajikistan Higher League") play in Dushanbe: [CSKA Pamir](/wiki/CSKA_Pamir_Dushanbe "CSKA Pamir Dushanbe"),^[\[243\]](#cite_note-247)^ [Dushanbe-83](/wiki/FC_Dushanbe-83 "FC Dushanbe-83"),^[\[244\]](#cite_note-248)^ [Istiklol](/wiki/FC_Istiklol "FC Istiklol"),^[\[245\]](#cite_note-249)^ and [Lokomotiv-Pamir](/wiki/FC_Lokomotiv-Pamir "FC Lokomotiv-Pamir").^[\[246\]](#cite_note-250)^ The [Pamir Stadium](/wiki/Pamir_Stadium "Pamir Stadium") in Dushanbe was constructed in 1939 where [CSKA Pamir Dushanbe](/wiki/CSKA_Pamir_Dushanbe "CSKA Pamir Dushanbe") played.^[\[247\]](#cite_note-251)^ [Dushanbe Stadium](/wiki/Dushanbe_Stadium "Dushanbe Stadium") is currently being constructed and will seat 30,000 when completed.^[\[248\]](#cite_note-252)^{#cite_ref-252}  

Media {#Media}
--------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dushanbe&action=edit&section=37 "Edit section: Media")\]  

### Newspapers and magazines {#Newspapers_and_magazines}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dushanbe&action=edit&section=38 "Edit section: Newspapers and magazines")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/%D8%B4%D9%85%D8%A7%D8%B1%D9%87_%DB%8C%DA%A9%D9%85_%D8%A8%D8%AE%D8%A7%D8%B1%D8%A7%DB%8C_%D8%B4%D8%B1%DB%8C%D9%81.jpg/220px-%D8%B4%D9%85%D8%A7%D8%B1%D9%87_%DB%8C%DA%A9%D9%85_%D8%A8%D8%AE%D8%A7%D8%B1%D8%A7%DB%8C_%D8%B4%D8%B1%DB%8C%D9%81.jpg)](/wiki/File:%D8%B4%D9%85%D8%A7%D8%B1%D9%87_%DB%8C%DA%A9%D9%85_%D8%A8%D8%AE%D8%A7%D8%B1%D8%A7%DB%8C_%D8%B4%D8%B1%DB%8C%D9%81.jpg) The front page of the first issue of *Bukhara Sharif* newspaper

The first newspaper published in Tajik was [*Bukhara Sharif*](/wiki/Bukharai-ye-sharif "Bukharai-ye-sharif") in [Kagan](/wiki/Kagan,_Uzbekistan "Kagan, Uzbekistan") on 11 March 1912 and published by leaders of the [Jadid movement](/wiki/Jadid_Movement "Jadid Movement") like Mirzo Jalol Yusufzoda. The purpose of the newspaper was to "be a scientific, literary, directional, subject, and economic publication that will strive for the spread of civilization and the idea." Soon after, however, [Ivan Petrov](/wiki/Ivan_Yefimovich_Petrov "Ivan Yefimovich Petrov") requested that the Emir of Bukhara close the paper, which he did on 2 January 1913.^[\[237\]](#cite_note-Mulloev-2009-241)^{#cite_ref-Mulloev-2009_241-2}

Oina and Mullo Nasreddin were two of the earliest Tajik language magazines. The *Zvezda Vostok* magazine was published in Tajik in the early 1920s in support of the October Revolution. The first Soviet newspaper distributed in Tajikistan was *Shulai Inkilob* (Flame of the Revolution) as propaganda for the Soviet government in 1919. It was distributed throughout Tajikistan and was the main Tajik language newspaper that opposed the previous Emirate and was clearly in support of communism, the [October Revolution](/wiki/October_Revolution "October Revolution"), and the [Bukharan Communist Party](/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Bukhara "Communist Party of Bukhara").^[\[237\]](#cite_note-Mulloev-2009-241)^{#cite_ref-Mulloev-2009_241-3}

The first Soviet newspaper published in Tajikistan was **Po basmachi** which detailed the conditions of the Red Army in Tajikistan in 1923 during the [Basmachi movement](/wiki/Basmachi_movement "Basmachi movement"). In 1924, the newspaper *Voice of the East* ([Russian](/wiki/Russian_language "Russian language"): Овози шарк or Голос Востока), the first Soviet government newspaper was published in Dushanbe and was a forum for much of the poetry and literature of the young republic. In 1925, the official newspaper of Soviet Tajikistan was "**Bedorii tochik** " (Awakening of the Tajiks). An Uzbek-language paper, Red Tajikistan, was published in Tajikistan as well. [Sadriddin Ayni](/wiki/Sadriddin_Ayni "Sadriddin Ayni") also published many newspapers such as *Bukhara News* , *Horpustak* , and *Flame of the Revolution* .^[\[237\]](#cite_note-Mulloev-2009-241)^{#cite_ref-Mulloev-2009_241-4}

In 1929, the newspaper Red Tajikistan came into print with a large daily circulation of 5000. In the 1930s *Komsomolets Tadzhikistana* was published as a communist paper intended for the youth of Tajikistan. Many other newspapers were published during this time as well. The press often emphasized the collective farming system and the newspaper *Dehkoni Kambagal* was popular among farmers.^[\[237\]](#cite_note-Mulloev-2009-241)^{#cite_ref-Mulloev-2009_241-5}

During World War 2 newspaper production was strained as raw materials became increasingly scarce and their numbers were reduced. After the war, the many newspapers from the 30s began to be produced once again. In the 60s and 70s the newspaper *Communist of Tajikistan* gained prominence, winning the [Order of the Red Banner of Labor](/wiki/Order_of_the_Red_Banner_of_Labour "Order of the Red Banner of Labour"). International cooperation was to be emphasized during the time period.^[\[237\]](#cite_note-Mulloev-2009-241)^{#cite_ref-Mulloev-2009_241-6}

During [perestroika](/wiki/Perestroika "Perestroika"), newspapers embraced more liberal and democratic ideas. One of the first to do this was the Komsomol of Tajikistan. Farkhang, a new literary magazine, published national Tajik and Islamic literature banned before such as the *[Masnavi](/wiki/Masnavi "Masnavi")* . The *Sukhan* newspaper, published by the Union of Journalists of Tajikistan, was a leading voice for liberalism and perestroika in the republic, writing about topics such as freedom of speech, democratization, and the opposition. The first publication not released by the state was from [Rastokhez](/wiki/Rastokhez "Rastokhez"), printed in Lithuania and delivered to Dushanbe. The [Democratic Party of Tajikistan](/wiki/Democratic_Party_(Tajikistan) "Democratic Party (Tajikistan)") published a paper, *Justice* , in Dushanbe as well which had a circulation of 25000. *Charogi Ruz* , or Light of Day, was the first private publication in Dushanbe, and advertised itself as the free tribune for youth. Free publications such as *Oinai zindagi* (by trade unions), *Somon* , *Haftgandzh* , and others formed.^[\[237\]](#cite_note-Mulloev-2009-241)^ Today, *Charogi Ruz* is known for its criticism of the ruling government.^[\[249\]](#cite_note-253)^{#cite_ref-253}

In August 1999 there were officially 199 newspapers, although only 17 of those appeared regularly. Some of the most widely circulated national government publications are *Dzhumhuriet* and *Narodna Gazeta* . In addition to the state news agency *[Khovar](/wiki/Khovar "Khovar")* (News), there are several private newspapers, including [Asia-Plus](/wiki/Asia-Plus "Asia-Plus"), which regularly publishes in Russian and English and reports on political, social and economic issues, *[Jumhuriyat](/wiki/Jumhuriyat "Jumhuriyat"),* and *[Khalk ovozi](/wiki/Khalk_ovozi "Khalk ovozi").^[\[250\]](#cite_note-ewy-254)^* ^[\[251\]](#cite_note-HRW-1999-255)^ In 2019 there were 37 regular newspapers and 37 magazines published in the city.^[\[5\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe-2021a-5)^{#cite_ref-Dushanbe-2021a_5-14}  

### Radio {#Radio}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dushanbe&action=edit&section=39 "Edit section: Radio")\]

In 1924 a radio station was built in Dushanbe for military communication. On 10 April 1930 the first radio broadcast was heard by civilians in Tajikistan, from Moscow. It functioned as a news source and a source of Soviet propaganda. The first station, in Dushanbe, mainly focused on retransmitted broadcasts from Moscow and radios gradually became more prevalent in the country. While development slowed during World War 2, afterwards Tajikistan received higher [broadband](/wiki/Broadband "Broadband") and quality radio stations and broadcasts.^[\[237\]](#cite_note-Mulloev-2009-241)^{#cite_ref-Mulloev-2009_241-8}

In 1977, locally created radio broadcasts were able to be transmitted from Dushanbe thanks to the construction of the Radio House in the city. In 2000, the Sadoi Dushanbe Radio was created, and today that is one of the four programs broadcast in Dushanbe.^[\[237\]](#cite_note-Mulloev-2009-241)^{#cite_ref-Mulloev-2009_241-9}

As of August 1999 government radio is broadcast throughout the nation along with independent outlets such as Asia Plus radio.^[\[239\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004g-243)^ [Radio Liberty](/wiki/Radio_Liberty "Radio Liberty"), the [BBC](/wiki/BBC "BBC"), and Sadoi Khuroson are also broadcast in Tajik, although no independent radio stations were in operation.^[\[251\]](#cite_note-HRW-1999-255)^{#cite_ref-HRW-1999_255-1}  

### Television {#Television}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dushanbe&action=edit&section=40 "Edit section: Television")\]

On 7 November 1959 the first television center was created in the republic, the [Tajik Television Studio](/wiki/Televizioni_Tojikiston "Televizioni Tojikiston"). In 1967 programs from Moscow and Tashkent were broadcast in the country and on 15 November 1975 color television was introduced.^[\[237\]](#cite_note-Mulloev-2009-241)^ As of August 1999 12 to 15 stations broadcast consistently. Many Russian language channels like ORT, RTR, and TV-6 broadcast as well.^[\[251\]](#cite_note-HRW-1999-255)^ Today, a greater number of private television stations operate in the city,^[\[239\]](#cite_note-Dushanbe_Encyc-2004g-243)^ with 15 in the whole country, although there are still 7 state owned channels.^[\[252\]](#cite_note-256)^{#cite_ref-256}  

Notable people {#Notable_people}
--------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dushanbe&action=edit&section=41 "Edit section: Notable people")\]

* [Zebo Aminzoda](/wiki/Zebo_Aminzoda "Zebo Aminzoda") (born 1948), Tajikistani ballet dancer and choreographer
* [Viktor Bout](/wiki/Viktor_Bout "Viktor Bout") (born 1967), Russian convicted arms dealer
* [Farruh Negmat-Zadeh](/wiki/Farruh_Negmat-Zadeh "Farruh Negmat-Zadeh") (born 1959), Tajikistani artist
* [Zoya Tajikova](/wiki/Zoya_Tajikova "Zoya Tajikova") (born 1935), Tajik musicologist
* [Vazgen Manasyan](/wiki/Vazgen_Manasyan "Vazgen Manasyan") (1958--2024), Tajikistani professional football coach and player of Armenian descent

International relations {#International_relations}
--------------------------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dushanbe&action=edit&section=42 "Edit section: International relations")\]  

### Twin towns -- sister cities {#Twin_towns_.E2.80.93_sister_cities}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dushanbe&action=edit&section=43 "Edit section: Twin towns – sister cities")\]  
See also: [List of twin towns and sister cities in Tajikistan](/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Asia#Tajikistan "List of twin towns and sister cities in Asia")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Boulder_Dushanbe_table.JPG/220px-Boulder_Dushanbe_table.JPG)](/wiki/File:Boulder_Dushanbe_table.JPG) Interior of the [Boulder Dushanbe teahouse](/wiki/Boulder_Dushanbe_teahouse "Boulder Dushanbe teahouse")

Dushanbe is [twinned](/wiki/Sister_city "Sister city") with:^[\[253\]](#cite_note-257)^{#cite_ref-257}  
* [![Turkey](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/23px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png)](/wiki/Turkey "Turkey") [Ankara](/wiki/Ankara "Ankara"), Turkey
* [![Turkmenistan](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Flag_of_Turkmenistan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Turkmenistan.svg.png)](/wiki/Turkmenistan "Turkmenistan") [Ashgabat](/wiki/Ashgabat "Ashgabat"), Turkmenistan
* [![Kazakhstan](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Flag_of_Kazakhstan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Kazakhstan.svg.png)](/wiki/Kazakhstan "Kazakhstan") [Astana](/wiki/Astana "Astana"), Kazakhstan
* [![Azerbaijan](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Flag_of_Azerbaijan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Azerbaijan.svg.png)](/wiki/Azerbaijan "Azerbaijan") [Baku](/wiki/Baku "Baku"), Azerbaijan
* [![United States](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png)](/wiki/United_States "United States") [Boulder](/wiki/Boulder,_Colorado "Boulder, Colorado"), United States
* [![Qatar](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Flag_of_Qatar.svg/23px-Flag_of_Qatar.svg.png)](/wiki/Qatar "Qatar") [Doha](/wiki/Doha "Doha"), Qatar
* [![China](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png)](/wiki/China "China") [Hainan](/wiki/Hainan "Hainan"), China
* [![Pakistan](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Flag_of_Pakistan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Pakistan.svg.png)](/wiki/Pakistan "Pakistan") [Islamabad](/wiki/Islamabad "Islamabad"), Pakistan
* [![Austria](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_Austria.svg/23px-Flag_of_Austria.svg.png)](/wiki/Austria "Austria") [Klagenfurt](/wiki/Klagenfurt "Klagenfurt"), Austria
* [![Pakistan](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Flag_of_Pakistan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Pakistan.svg.png)](/wiki/Pakistan "Pakistan") [Lahore](/wiki/Lahore "Lahore"), Pakistan
* [![Zambia](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Flag_of_Zambia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Zambia.svg.png)](/wiki/Zambia "Zambia") [Lusaka](/wiki/Lusaka "Lusaka"), Zambia
* [![Afghanistan](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Flag_of_the_Taliban.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Taliban.svg.png)](/wiki/Afghanistan "Afghanistan") [Mazar-i-Sharif](/wiki/Mazar-i-Sharif "Mazar-i-Sharif"), Afghanistan
* [![Belarus](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Flag_of_Belarus.svg/23px-Flag_of_Belarus.svg.png)](/wiki/Belarus "Belarus") [Minsk](/wiki/Minsk "Minsk"), Belarus
* [![Tunisia](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Flag_of_Tunisia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Tunisia.svg.png)](/wiki/Tunisia "Tunisia") [Monastir](/wiki/Monastir,_Tunisia "Monastir, Tunisia"), Tunisia
* [![China](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png)](/wiki/China "China") [Qingdao](/wiki/Qingdao "Qingdao"), China
* [![Germany](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/23px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png)](/wiki/Germany "Germany") [Reutlingen](/wiki/Reutlingen "Reutlingen"), Germany
* [![Russia](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png)](/wiki/Russia "Russia") [Saint Petersburg](/wiki/Saint_Petersburg "Saint Petersburg"), Russia
* [![Yemen](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Flag_of_Yemen.svg/23px-Flag_of_Yemen.svg.png)](/wiki/Yemen "Yemen") [Sanaa](/wiki/Sanaa "Sanaa"), Yemen
* [![Iran](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Flag_of_Iran.svg/23px-Flag_of_Iran.svg.png)](/wiki/Iran "Iran") [Shiraz](/wiki/Shiraz "Shiraz"), Iran
* [![Iran](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Flag_of_Iran.svg/23px-Flag_of_Iran.svg.png)](/wiki/Iran "Iran") [Tehran](/wiki/Tehran "Tehran"), Iran
* [![China](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png)](/wiki/China "China") [Ürümqi](/wiki/%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi "Ürümqi"), China
* [![China](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png)](/wiki/China "China") [Xiamen](/wiki/Xiamen "Xiamen"), China

In 1982, Mary Hey and Sophia Stoller started an initiative to make Dushanbe a sister city of [Boulder](/wiki/Boulder,_Colorado "Boulder, Colorado") even though during that time they were on opposite sides of the [Cold War](/wiki/Cold_War "Cold War"). In 1987, the mayor of Dushanbe, [Maksud Ikramov](/w/index.php?title=Maksud_Ikramov&action=edit&redlink=1 "Maksud Ikramov (page does not exist)"), officially made Boulder a sister city of Dushanbe. Exchange students, tourism, and art exchanges began between the two cities. The [Tajik Teahouse](/wiki/Dushanbe_Tea_House "Dushanbe Tea House") was sent from Dushanbe to Boulder in 1990. During the [civil war](/wiki/Tajikistani_Civil_War "Tajikistani Civil War"), Boulder sent humanitarian aid to Dushanbe.^[\[254\]](#cite_note-258)^{#cite_ref-258}  

### International conferences {#International_conferences}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Dushanbe&action=edit&section=44 "Edit section: International conferences")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Dmitry_Medvedev_28_August_2008-5.jpg/135px-Dmitry_Medvedev_28_August_2008-5.jpg)](/wiki/File:Dmitry_Medvedev_28_August_2008-5.jpg) 2008 Shanghai Coordination Council meeting.

Many international conferences have been held in Dushanbe, such as the International Conference on Integrated [TB](/wiki/Tuberculosis "Tuberculosis") Control in Central Asia^[\[255\]](#cite_note-259)^ and the hosting of the [Shanghai Cooperation Organization](/wiki/Shanghai_Cooperation_Organisation "Shanghai Cooperation Organisation") conference in 2000, 2008, and [2014](/wiki/2014_SCO_summit "2014 SCO summit").^[\[256\]](#cite_note-260)^^[\[257\]](#cite_note-261)^^[\[258\]](#cite_note-262)^{#cite_ref-262}

In 2003, Dushanbe hosted the International Forum on Fresh Water which was attended by 50 states and organizations.^[\[259\]](#cite_note-263)^^[\[260\]](#cite_note-264)^{#cite_ref-264}

From 20 to 23 June 2018 the High-Level International Conference on the International Decade for Action 'Water for Sustainable Development' was held in Dushanbe, which discussed the upcoming decade for action with regards to water.^[\[261\]](#cite_note-265)^ A second conference on the same subject was planned to be held in June 2020.^[\[262\]](#cite_note-266)^{#cite_ref-266}

On 16--17 May 2019 a high-level conference entitled "Countering Terrorism and its Financing Through [Illicit Drug Trafficking](/wiki/Illicit_drug_trafficking "Illicit drug trafficking") and Organized Crime" was held in Dushanbe and attended by more than 50 countries. It passed the Dushanbe declaration, which put the primary responsibility for fighting terrorism onto national governments. Other topics, such as drug smuggling, were also discussed.^[\[263\]](#cite_note-267)^{#cite_ref-267}

On 15 June 2019 the fifth summit of the [Conference on Interaction and Confidence-Building Measures in Asia](/wiki/Conference_on_Interaction_and_Confidence-Building_Measures_in_Asia "Conference on Interaction and Confidence-Building Measures in Asia") was held in Dushanbe. The Asian members of the organization discussed common interests on topics such as peace and security, terrorism, arms control, the [Iran nuclear deal](/wiki/Joint_Comprehensive_Plan_of_Action "Joint Comprehensive Plan of Action"), poverty, economic development, and [globalization](/wiki/Globalization "Globalization").^[\[264\]](#cite_note-268)^{#cite_ref-268}

263. **[\^](#cite_ref-267)** ["UNRCCA and UNOCT Participated in the High-Level Conference "Countering Terrorism and Its Financing Through Illicit Drug Trafficking and Organized Crime" in Dushanbe, 16-17 May 2019"](https://unrcca.unmissions.org/unrcca-and-unoct-participated-high-level-conference-%E2%80%9Ccountering-terrorism-and-its-financing-through). *UNRCCA* . 20 May 2019. Retrieved 10 August 2020.{#cite_note-267}

PTI. 15 June 2019. [ISSN](/wiki/ISSN_(identifier) "ISSN (identifier)") [0971-751X](https://search.worldcat.org/issn/0971-751X). Retrieved 5 March 2021.{#cite_note-268}
